<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a5804848-5690-4e0a-bfe6-4e9c35699c43'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText14672310734262217712" style="display:none">In this classic novel of two willful lovers caught in a breathless adventure of deception and betrayal, #1 New York Times bestselling author Judith McNaught has created a powerful and unforgettable masterpiece.<br /><br />ELIZABETH CAMERON<br /><br />The Countess of Havenhurst possessed a rare gentleness and fierce courage to match her exquisite beauty. But her reputation is shattered when she is discovered in the arms of Ian Thornton, a notorious gambler and social outcast.<br /><br />IAN THORNTON<br /><br />A dangerously handsome man of secret wealth and mysterious lineage, his voyage to Elizabeth's heart is fraught with intrigue, scandal, and a venomous revenge.<br /><br />Destined for each other, yet wary of each other's motives, Elizabeth and Ian engage in a dance of suspicion and passion that tests the very soul of their star-crossed love. As a twisting path of secrets takes them from London's drawing rooms to the mysterious Scottish Highlands, Elizabeth must learn the truth: is Ian merely a ruthless fortune hunter at heart?</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1482252-what-does-this-dialogue-exchanged-between">What does this dialogue exchanged between Ian and Elizabeth means:

&#39;&#39;There are four steps separating us and a year and a half of wanting drawing us together,” he said. 

Elizabeth swallowed. “Couldn&#39;t you meet me halfway?&#39;&#39;</a>
</div>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/61625972-emanuellen-trizi"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1479328003i/61625972._UY100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/61625972-emanuellen-trizi">Emanuellen Trizi</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">If I remember correctly, its because they finally are in the same room, only four steps apart. But they were missing each other because the two of the<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">If I remember correctly, its because they finally are in the same room, only four steps apart. But they were missing each other because the two of them were too strong-minded and proud to say what they hearts desires in some fight along the book, so they stood a long time apart, he in Scotland and he in London (if I remember correctly). When Elizabeth asks him to meet her halfway, I believe its a way of both of them to compromise instead of one of them has to give up pride. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

    <a title="Dina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1918270-dina"><img alt="Dina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460302951p2/1918270.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45277647?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dina" href="/user/show/1918270-dina">Dina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Dina by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2592043-k">K.</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1918270-dina?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1918270-dina?shelf=dik">dik</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45277647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer191876967534464338">I absolutely LOVE this book! This is what I posted at the RF (Amazon) when I read it for the 1st time, and I'm simply copying my post here on GR because I'm lazy and don't feel like writing a full review...<br/><br/>Well, I've just finished reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/129621.Almost_Heaven' title='Almost Heaven by Judith McNaught' rel='nofollow noopener'>Almost Heaven</a> and I'm glad to say that I'm in love with Ian, Elizabeth, and everyone and everything else in the book. :) I especially loved Ian for having no fear admitting to himself he was in love with Elizabeth without knowing if she felt the same, and I ado</span>
  <span id="freeText191876967534464338" style="display:none">I absolutely LOVE this book! This is what I posted at the RF (Amazon) when I read it for the 1st time, and I'm simply copying my post here on GR because I'm lazy and don't feel like writing a full review...<br /><br />Well, I've just finished reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/129621.Almost_Heaven" title="Almost Heaven by Judith McNaught" rel="nofollow noopener">Almost Heaven</a> and I'm glad to say that I'm in love with Ian, Elizabeth, and everyone and everything else in the book. :) I especially loved Ian for having no fear admitting to himself he was in love with Elizabeth without knowing if she felt the same, and I adored Elizabeth for standing her ground and not cowering when Ian tried to send her away.<br /><br />I though the Big Misunderstanding issue would turn me off because I'm not a fan of this kind of plot device - and there were not only one, but two in this book -, but JM made it believable to me. Ian and Elizabeth were so much in love with each other that it rendered them defenseless, insecure and wary. The more you love someone, the more you're open to being hurt by them.<br /><br />Quoting Elizabeth: <i>"I've hurt you terribly, my love, and I'll hurt you again during the next fifty years. And you are going to hurt me, Ian - never, I hope, as much as you are hurting me now. But if that's the way it has to be, then I'll endure it, because the only alternative is to live without you, and that is no life at all."</i> Oh my!<br /><br />And I can't resist adding my favorite passage:<br /><br /><i>"If you would take one step forward, darling, you could cry in my arms. And while you do, I'll tell you how sorry I am for everything I've done -" Unable to wait, Ian caught her, pulling her tightly against him. "And when I'm finished," he whispered hoarsely as she wrapped her arms around him and wept brokenly, "you can help me find a way to forgive myself."<br /><br />Tortured by her tears, he clasped her tighter and rubbed his jaw against her temple, his voice a ravaged whisper: "I'm sorry," he told her. He cupped her face between his palms, tipping it up and gazing into her eyes, his thumbs moving over her wet cheeks. "I'm sorry." Slowly, he bent his head, covering her mouth with his. "I'm so damned sorry."</i><br /><br />OMG, I cried when I read that! And I'm not ashamed to say, my eyes are "suspiciously bright" right now, while I'm typing this...<br /><br />I'll stop now. Otherwise, I'll just end up posting every single line of dialogue exchanged between Ian and Elizabeth. :)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="191876967534464338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_743209758" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/743209758" />
    <a title="Mo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11856352-mo"><img alt="Mo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1371247812p2/11856352.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/743209758?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mo" href="/user/show/11856352-mo">Mo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer743209758" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11719812476563224934"><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454705200ra/18003237.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Another re-read. Another hit. Seriously, Ms McNaught is the Queen of Historical fiction ... well in this series anyway. I do think she left the best 'til last, even though I did love the first two in the series also. Ian. Ian, Ian, Ian ... I think I loved Ian more than Jordon and Jason (although while I was reading about them, I was totally in love with them) - maybe it is because Ian is a Commoner ... and he is Scottish, well, half-Scottish. I do love Scotland. I have already reviewed the book </span>
  <span id="freeText11719812476563224934" style="display:none"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454705200ra/18003237.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Another re-read. Another hit. Seriously, Ms McNaught is the Queen of Historical fiction ... well in this series anyway. I do think she left the best 'til last, even though I did love the first two in the series also. Ian. Ian, Ian, Ian ... I think I loved Ian more than Jordon and Jason (although while I was reading about them, I was totally in love with them) - maybe it is because Ian is a Commoner ... and he is Scottish, well, half-Scottish. I do love Scotland. I have already reviewed the book on first reading it, so won't bore you anymore. It's such a pity that this author doesn't write Historicals anymore. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487947809i/22067372._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And that Epilogue. I have said it before and I'll say it again, "every book should have an epilogue".<br><br><br> <b>ORIGINAL REVIEW IS BELOW </b><br>********************************************************<br><br>Five Heavenly Stars. If I could give it more stars, I would.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402492037i/9945173.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>Elizabeth Cameron, with her angelic beauty, golden hair and shining green eyes, had taken London by storm. <br>She was not a rage She was <i>the</i> rage</b>
  <b></b>
</blockquote><br><br>I could not put this book down. I am not sure if any review can do it justice. I think it might have become one of my favourite books ever.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402491206i/9945009._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>”Look, Elizabeth, isn’t he divine in a sort of mysterious, wicked way?”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Divine, divine you say. Ian, Ian, Ian, I loved you. Such a torturned hero. I felt for him. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1402021595ra/9883698.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I really don’t want to say much about the storyline as it is a wonderfully woven tale that is best discovered by yourselves.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>”I think,” he said softly, “that you are magnificent.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Their love story is not a straightforward tale. There are trials and tribulations, misunderstandings, lies, mistrusts. It had it all. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1402491206ra/9945010.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>But it was worth it. I swear I could literally start the book from the beginning straight away. I loved it that much. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“Elizabeth’s entire body started to tremble as his lips began descending to hers. and she sought to forestall what her heart knew was inevitable by reasoning with him. “A gently bred Englishwoman,” she shakily quoted Lucinda’s lecture. “feels nothing stronger than affection. We do not fall in love.” <br><br>His warm lips covered hers. “I’m a Scot,” he murmured huskily. “We do.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402491206i/9945011._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>”Dance with me, Elizabeth.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402491206i/9945014._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And for this of you who think there are NO sex scenes in Historicals... there are. And very nice they are too.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1402491206ra/9945013.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>“Because,” he said quietly as she stood up, “until you walked into it, this was an ordinary garden.”<br><br>Puzzled, Elizabeth tipped her head. “What is it now?” <br><br>“Heaven.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402491206i/9945012.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I loved meeting with Jordan and Alex from the previous book… and the Dowager!<br><br>I wish Ms McNaught would write more Historicals. I know she has written contemporaries also but I think she shines in the Historical genre.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>The sight that Ian beheld when he looked up make his grin fade as tenderness and awe shook through him. Spread out before him in colorful splendor were the most magnificent flower gardens I an had ever beheld. The other heirs of Havenhurst night have added stone and mortar to the house, but Elizaebeth had given it breathtaking beauty.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402491206i/9945015._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>It was the longest three weeks of his life. <br>It was the shortest of hers</b>
</blockquote><br><br>I feel I could wax lyrical about this book for ages and ages but I’d better not. As I have said before to those of you who do NOT read historicals, please give them a try. The three books in this series have been solid FIVE stars, if not more for me.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402491206i/9945016._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And I got my Epilogue. And what a wonderful Epilogue it was. It was Heaven.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1100427279" />
    <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6972914-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529600203p2/6972914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1100427279?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/6972914-karen">Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6972914-karen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1100427279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3976649462152863712"><b>5 SOLID STARS ★★★★★</b><br/><span>[image error]</span><a href='http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects/m1ny5b8qjikq.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416022539i/11877946._SY540_.jpg' alt=' photo m1ny5b8qjikq.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Because,” he said quietly as she stood up, <br/>“until you walked into it, this was an ordinary garden.”<br/>Puzzled, Elizabeth tipped her head. “What is it now?” <br/>“Heaven.”</i>
</b> <br/><br/>And… once again, I am SPEECHLESS!!! Words just can not express the love I have for Judith McNaught and her incredible books. And with such appropriate titles. Every time I finish one, I want to flip back to the beginning and read it all over again. I am convinced that NO ONE can write a romantic</span>
  <span id="freeText3976649462152863712" style="display:none"><b>5 SOLID STARS ★★★★★</b><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects/m1ny5b8qjikq.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416022539i/11877946._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo m1ny5b8qjikq.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>“Because,” he said quietly as she stood up, <br>“until you walked into it, this was an ordinary garden.”<br>Puzzled, Elizabeth tipped her head. “What is it now?” <br>“Heaven.”</i>
</b> <br><br>And… once again, I am SPEECHLESS!!! Words just can not express the love I have for Judith McNaught and her incredible books. And with such appropriate titles. Every time I finish one, I want to flip back to the beginning and read it all over again. I am convinced that NO ONE can write a romantic character as well. …the arrogance, the depth of feeling …the intelligence, strength and wit are just astounding. Not to mention the battle of wills and the angst that always sets the characters against each other, bounding through fields of torment and longing, love and self-loathing …absolutely FUCKING BRILLIANT!!!<br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Women/amanda-seyfried-cle-de-peau-beaute-2014-campaign3.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416022539i/11877947._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo amanda-seyfried-cle-de-peau-beaute-2014-campaign3.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Lady Elizabeth Cameron</b>, the Countess of Havenhurst, was a rare beauty. She had a face that could bring any man to his knees, but she also possessed immeasurable grace, wit and charm, innocence and pride. She was gentle, loyal, and incredibly courageous for someone so young. But surpassing all of these desirable qualities were the most captivating emerald eyes Ian Thornton had ever seen. <br><br>Losing both her parents by the time she was seventeen, Elizabeth had been left, along with her half-brother Robert Cameron to manage their family’s estate. But large gambling debts incurred by both her late father and her brother, had left Havenhurst stripped of it’s former splendor. Trying desperately to save her family’s legacy, Elizabeth is left to manage the estate on her own, and suffer the pursuit by numerous debtors.<br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects/af8a2b291df2db47972eba8e8d22041f.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1410104266i/11062568._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo af8a2b291df2db47972eba8e8d22041f.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Meanwhile, Robert Cameron, her half-brother, and her Uncle Julius, have decided that an advantageous marriage to a wealthy and titled suitor just might solve all of the families financial troubles. So she is to be presented in London's finest society functions, where the <i>ton's</i> most elibible bachelors will be gathering to select a wife.<br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects/P-P-1995-Screencaps-Random-pride-and-prejudice-1995-6148851-1024-576-1.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415734423i/11837628._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo P-P-1995-Screencaps-Random-pride-and-prejudice-1995-6148851-1024-576-1.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Elizabeth is a smashing success, and receives an unprecedented number of offers for her hand. But while Robert is busy squaring up the betrothal agreement for Viscount Mondevale’s offer, Elizabeth is off wandering through the gardens at a society party and unknowingly catching the eye of yet another gentleman.<br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Men/e29beb6b-b3fe-4dbd-ad9e-ea67e1a75ce1.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385954790i/7264789.jpg" alt=" photo e29beb6b-b3fe-4dbd-ad9e-ea67e1a75ce1.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Ian Thornton</b> is a notoriously wealthy, and dangerously handsome man. Rumored to be the bastard son of the Marquess of Kensington, he has earned a reputation as a high-stakes gambler, and a ruthless businessman as well as an unspeakable rake. He is not well respected as a gentleman, and is frequently the subject of malicious gossip amongst the ton. But he is also quite charming and often irresistible to the ladies. And Elizabeth is no exception.<br><br>Caught completely unaware of his questionable reputation, Elizabeth is pressured by her new found friends to coax him into dancing with her. Little did she know that her association with him was going to change her life forever. <br><br><b>
  <i> “And as to needing to know who I am, that’s very simple to answer.” His hand lifted, grazing her pale cheek, then smoothing backward, cupping her head. Gently he explained, “I am the man you’re going to marry.”</i>
</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects/c3.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416022539i/11877949.jpg" alt=" photo c3.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i> “Your eyes are more lethal than dueling pistols, my sweet.” he said wryly. “They could make a saint forget his goal.”</i>
</b><br><br>And as it goes, seizing on their opportunity, Elizabeth’s jealous friends, maliciously set her up for a scandal that will tear her down, ruin her reputation, and destroy any chances she might have had at landing a husband. <br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Couples/017e354d-0b8a-4617-9be5-ab3aa2cc7072.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416022539i/11877950._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 017e354d-0b8a-4617-9be5-ab3aa2cc7072.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>When he finally dragged his mouth from hers Ian kept his arms around her,<br>and Elizabeth laid her cheek against his crisp white shirt, <br>feeling his lips brush the hair atop her head.<br>“That was an even bigger mistake than I feared it would be,” he said, and then he added almost absently, <br>“God help us both.”</i>
</b><br><br>And the results are catastrophic! Not only are her offers withdrawn, but duels are waged, blood is spilled, and reputations are ruined. Elizabeth’s brother is so enraged by the turn of events and the advances of this notorious blackguard, that he goes on a murderous rampage to defend her honor, and then just disappears leaving Elizabeth alone to pick up the pieces of her shattered life. With mounting debts and little left of her reputation, Elizabeth must find a way to survive on her own, and find some way of keeping her family's estate from the auctioners block. <br><br><b>
  <i> “Dying over an argument isn’t honor, it’s a waste of a man’s life.”</i>
</b><br><br>AND that is just the introduction… I loved every minute of this story! Good and bad. So much scandal and passion, so many regrets. And Ian… sweet baby Jesus, Ian Thornton …so in love with the girl he can barely control his wits, yet so incredibly prideful that he won’t EVER be made of fool of. He leaves her to her fate.<br><br>Oh, there will be a HEA.. but it will tear your heart out first, chew it up and spit it out. And you will beg for more. <br><br><b>
  <i>His gaze held hers, and his voice was tender and rough. “Love me, Elizabeth.”</i>
</b><br><br>What a story! I could go on and on, but I’ve already said too much. I was on the edge of my seat the entire time! Watching like a hungry voyeur. I can say no more. I am choked up with joyous exultation. Ok… maybe that was laying it on a bit thick. But you get my meaning.<br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects/9a138af504a27b4e1029f23a48f1d37e.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416022539i/11877951._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 9a138af504a27b4e1029f23a48f1d37e.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i> “If you would take one step forward, darling, you could cry in my arms. And while you do, I’ll tell you how sorry I am for everything I’ve done.”</i>
</b><br><br>I highly recommend all of these incredible books to anyone who has a love of love, unforgettable dialogue and great writing. This is ROMANCE PORN in it’s most explicit 19th century form. <br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects/1795LMcM3.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416022539i/11877952.jpg" alt=" photo 1795LMcM3.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3976649462152863712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5498948-lana-dg-romance"><img alt="Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376622739p2/5498948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2452204032?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾" href="/user/show/5498948-lana-dg-romance">Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32491312-almost-heaven">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=favorite-alpha-hero">favorite-alpha-hero</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2452204032" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15589260487634201950"><b>5 STARS</b><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png' width='50' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>There are four steps separating us and a year and a half of wanting drawing us together,” he said. Elizabeth swallowed. “Couldn’t you meet me halfway?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1519890078ra/25141789.gif' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>All.<br/>Of.<br/>The.<br/>Swoons.<br/><br/>This. THIS is exactly why I love historical romances. And it's also why I'm currently kicking myself for only discovering this incredible author now. There's only one thing I love more than a good bastard in a romance, and that's a redeemable bastard that's not afraid to wear his heart on his sleeve when he fin</span>
  <span id="freeText15589260487634201950" style="display:none"><b>5 STARS</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">There are four steps separating us and a year and a half of wanting drawing us together,” he said. Elizabeth swallowed. “Couldn’t you meet me halfway?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1519890078ra/25141789.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>All.<br>Of.<br>The.<br>Swoons.<br><br>This. THIS is exactly why I love historical romances. And it's also why I'm currently kicking myself for only discovering this incredible author now. There's only one thing I love more than a good bastard in a romance, and that's a redeemable bastard that's not afraid to wear his heart on his sleeve when he finally sees the error of his ways. Even if that particular feet takes him the majority of the book to do. <br><br>Almost Heaven is the story of a young beauty just entering London society in search for a husband that will save her beloved estate, and a man that's always been the source of most gossip within it. Ian is known as a scoundrel, a gambler, anything but the titled husband Elizabeth needs. He's also a beautifully dangerous enigma that draws her like a moth to a flame. Until she gets too close and they both get burned.<br><br>This was a delicious tale of secrets and betrayal, of mistakes and forgiveness, but ultimately of a love that prevails against all odds. It was WONDERFULLY swoony. <br><br>At first I was a little concerned because Elizabeth and Ian get together so quickly. I'm not usually a fan of quick coupling. I was yearning for angst and emotion. I shouldn't have been concerned, because their initial meeting was only the calm before the storm. And what a storm it was! Ian is a downright bastard to Elizabeth when they meet again two years after the fateful first time. GOD BUT I LOVED IT! But it's no secret that I love the bastards. Elizabeth was an incredible heroine. She's young and sheltered, but she's clever and smart and so endearing. I loved her strength and her sharp wit. She's not afraid to stand up for herself, but she also knows that sometimes the biggest fight requires a sacrifice. She was the perfect match to the broody and enigmatic Ian.<br><br>The story was phenomenal and kept me glued to the pages long into the night. I NEEDED to see how it all unveils and I couldn't be more satisfied. This is going down as one of my favorite historical romances. And that epilogue?! SWOON!!!!<br><br><b>Find me on:<br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/DirtyGirlRomance?" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436986543i/15525717.png" width="40" height="40" alt="Follow me on facebook" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> <a href="https://twitter.com/DirtyGrlRomance" target="twitter" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436986543i/15525718.png" width="40" height="40" alt="Follow Me on Twitter" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> <a href="http://www.dirtygirlromance.com" target="blog" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436986543i/15525719.png" width="40" height="40" alt="blog" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><a href="http://dirtygirlromance.com" target="blog" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1530810453i/25928532._SX540_.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></b></span>

<div id="review_80882680" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/80882680" />
    <a title="Rane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1987431-rane"><img alt="Rane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419878997p2/1987431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/80882680?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rane" href="/user/show/1987431-rane">Rane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780671742553" href="/book/show/534564.Almost_Heaven">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Rane by: </span>
      Dina
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=regency-napoleonic-era">regency-napoleonic-era</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=keeper">keeper</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer80882680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4362912976288700746">There’s been many books I can say I couldn’t put down, but I can truly say there’s also been just a handful of books where it was sometimes physical impossible to stop reading, and putting the book away. Almost Heaven by Judith McNaught was one of those books. Through the hardships,tears and yes, misunderstandings I couldn’t put this book down, I wanted, no <i>needed</i> to keep reading to find out what happen next to these two amazing leads.<br/><br/> Elizabeth Cameron was one of those heroine’s you love on the</span>
  <span id="freeText4362912976288700746" style="display:none">There’s been many books I can say I couldn’t put down, but I can truly say there’s also been just a handful of books where it was sometimes physical impossible to stop reading, and putting the book away. Almost Heaven by Judith McNaught was one of those books. Through the hardships,tears and yes, misunderstandings I couldn’t put this book down, I wanted, no <i>needed</i> to keep reading to find out what happen next to these two amazing leads.<br /><br /> Elizabeth Cameron was one of those heroine’s you love on the spot, she was smart, beautiful but she had most of all courage and bountiful amounts of love to give. After having her uncle force her hand in an unwanted marriages, Elizabeth is face once again with her past, one where in order to save her home and her brother from debts she was to get married to a rich, kind man and she felt foolish enough to fall in love whom she thought was the wrong man and only wanted her for a quick tumble in the sheets, and with a vengeful friend out to destroy her, Elizabeth’s reputation was in ruins. Elizabeth without her brother whom up and left and only her home to go back to, keeps moving on. Elizabeth may have been brought down to a low, but she was strong enough to face whatever came her way, and it’s her strength that shows many of times, as she has to fight many battles along the way, but she stays strong and keeps hope in her heart. <br /> <br /> Ian Thornton, Ian, how I adore thee. Ian was one of those men you wish you could meet in real life, he felt so real at times, I thought he just jump off the pages, where I could yell at him for being mule-headed but hold him when he was hurting. Ian was at times such a complex man and at times so simple. Ian’s life hasn’t been a bed of roses, the son of a disowned peer and a sister of a Scottish vicar, Ian’s life was quickly turn to the worse when his family suddenly die in a fire. Ian goes through life making gambles and money hand over fist, but never truly happy, until he finds love and heartbreak with Elizabeth. Ian like Elizabeth get caught in a tangle of misunderstandings, but these misunderstandings bring them back together. Ian is very open about his passion and later his love of Elizabeth and shy about himself. Ian was at times heartbreaking sweet and mule-headed pain in the butt, but I loved learning about him every second, and I loved him deeply. <br /><br /> Ian and Elizabeth have a long road ahead of them, and it’s their love and their forgiveness that heal their hearts and the sadly the wounds they inflicted on one another through things beyond their control, but their love was stronger and able to overcome their hundles and find peace and love in one another.<br /><br /> There was so many memorable characters plotted around the story, from Elizabeth’s childhood friend Alex to Ian old time friend Jack but my favorites were Lucy- Elizabeth’s companion, who may have been stern but had a quick witted mind and knew how to handle a mean horse. And Ian’s grandfather who knew his mistake and wanted to make it up not only to Ian’s father, but to Ian himself, and was willing to let go of his pride in the end to do that.<br /><br /><br />Overall: This book was beautiful from start to finish and yes, I have I did cry buckets, but more often then not they were tears of joys as two great souls Ian and Elizabeth finding one another. This book wasn’t Almost Heaven to read but truly Heavenly!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4362912976288700746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1281922434" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1281922434" />
    <a title="Danielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22412202-danielle"><img alt="Danielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533861300p2/22412202.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1281922434?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle" href="/user/show/22412202-danielle">Danielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22412202-danielle?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22412202-danielle?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22412202-danielle?shelf=epic">epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22412202-danielle?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22412202-danielle?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22412202-danielle?shelf=couldnt-put-down">couldnt-put-down</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22412202-danielle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22412202-danielle?shelf=enemies-to-lovers">enemies-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22412202-danielle?shelf=angsty">angsty</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1281922434" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15777956664914585728">I'm pretty sure - but not positive - that Judith McNaught is actually a god-like being who writes romance from the sky, just for me. <br/><br/>Now, maybe that's a little presumptuous of me, but eh, how else could she know how to make me love every one of her books? <br/><br/>You have another idea? Didn't think so. <br/><br/>Just like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/350684.Whitney__My_Love__Westmoreland___2_' title='Whitney, My Love (Westmoreland, #2) by Judith McNaught' rel='nofollow noopener'>Whitney, My Love</a> or <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/129619.A_Kingdom_of_Dreams__Westmoreland___1_' title='A Kingdom of Dreams (Westmoreland, #1) by Judith McNaught' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Kingdom of Dreams</a>, <b>Almost Heaven</b> is deeply developed, with dimensional characters full of sizzling chemistry - whose romance grows on you until it burns into your heart. <br/><br/>Th</span>
  <span id="freeText15777956664914585728" style="display:none">I'm pretty sure - but not positive - that Judith McNaught is actually a god-like being who writes romance from the sky, just for me. <br /><br />Now, maybe that's a little presumptuous of me, but eh, how else could she know how to make me love every one of her books? <br /><br />You have another idea? Didn't think so. <br /><br />Just like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/350684.Whitney__My_Love__Westmoreland___2_" title="Whitney, My Love (Westmoreland, #2) by Judith McNaught" rel="nofollow noopener">Whitney, My Love</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/129619.A_Kingdom_of_Dreams__Westmoreland___1_" title="A Kingdom of Dreams (Westmoreland, #1) by Judith McNaught" rel="nofollow noopener">A Kingdom of Dreams</a>, <b>Almost Heaven</b> is deeply developed, with dimensional characters full of sizzling chemistry - whose romance grows on you until it burns into your heart. <br /><br />This hero. <i>Lord have mercy.</i><br /><br />I'm not one for sweet heroes, and I was unsure - even though he had an intoxicating presence about him - how much I was going to love a hero who immediately proposes to the heroine, while professing to her that's she "magnificent." Well, I should have known right away (this is Judith McNaught folks, Queen of Conflict) that their amicable relationship wouldn't last long, and that their short 'tryst' actually became a nightmare for the heroine. <br /><br />I don't particularly like to read about couples who have already met before - at least in a romantic way - and neither do I like flashbacks to show the scene we weren't there to witness. But McNaught does it in a way that makes it feel like it's the present, and the first meeting between Ian and Elizabeth was electric - Ian, a more handsome than sin scoundrel without a title nor fortune to keep him in the ton's good graces. <br /><br />If it wouldn't come off strange, I would write this entire review swooning over just how hot this hero actually is. But, alas, that might make me come off as a lonely creeper. <br /><br />Confidence. Intelligence. An electric sex appeal. Ian had it all. He went from poor to riches. There is nothing more attractive than an ambitious man - and that is exactly what he was. At one point he was aspiring to marry a stunning, intelligent debutante who he met briefly during a weekend party, until he found out she was cuckolding her fiance by looking for a fling with him - or so he thought. <br /><br />Two years later, Elizabeth's in dire straights, about to lose her home she has spent the past years stringing pennies along to keep. She's a social outcast from being caught up in the scandal with Ian, and she wants nothing more than to never see him again. But little does she know her uncle has written her past suitors to try to marry her off again. Ian being one of them, but only because his incompetent servant agreed to the wrong letter. <br /><br />Elizabeth was a fierce, intelligent heroine. Her hatred of Ian is greatly returned, and when she shows up on his doorstep in rural Scotland, they both didn't think they'd be pulled together like they had that very first time two years past. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/129621.Almost_Heaven__Sequels___3_" title="Almost Heaven (Sequels, #3) by Judith McNaught" rel="nofollow noopener">Almost Heaven</a> was so much fun. I found myself trying to quell my laughter so my husband didn't wake up - and yes, I stayed up way too late to finish it. The chemistry between the couple was electric - hell, Ian was eletric himself, and there was an abundance of conflict to keep me stuck to the pages. A fantastic tale by JM going straight to my favorites' shelf.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15777956664914585728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2033593292" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2033593292" />
    <a title="Ivy H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56605398-ivy-h"><img alt="Ivy H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513871125p2/56605398.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2033593292?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivy H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivy H" href="/user/show/56605398-ivy-h">Ivy H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32491312-almost-heaven">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56605398-ivy-h?shelf=sexy-hot-hero">sexy-hot-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56605398-ivy-h?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56605398-ivy-h?shelf=the-perfect-couple">the-perfect-couple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56605398-ivy-h?shelf=broody-hero-with-tortured-past">broody-hero-with-tortured-past</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56605398-ivy-h?shelf=hero-was-a-stubborn-asshole">hero-was-a-stubborn-asshole</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56605398-ivy-h?shelf=virginal-heroine">virginal-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56605398-ivy-h?shelf=feisty-funny-heroine">feisty-funny-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56605398-ivy-h?shelf=hero-is-heroine-s-only-lover">hero-is-heroine-s-only-lover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56605398-ivy-h?shelf=second-chance-romance">second-chance-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56605398-ivy-h?shelf=beautiful-heroine">beautiful-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2033593292&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2033593292" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3141084665909108619">Every lover of romance novels has got that <b>one special story</b> that's #1 in her eyes; it's the novel that always tops all others with MC's who are a head and shoulders above all the other favourites. Well, Judith McNaught is my favourite romance novelist of all time and this novel is my special #1. I've read this about 4 or 5 times ( perhaps even more ) ever since I first borrowed a copy from my aunt almost a decade or so ago. It was perfect and heart wrenchingly romantic. It's as much a timeless </span>
  <span id="freeText3141084665909108619" style="display:none">Every lover of romance novels has got that <b>one special story</b> that's #1 in her eyes; it's the novel that always tops all others with MC's who are a head and shoulders above all the other favourites. Well, Judith McNaught is my favourite romance novelist of all time and this novel is my special #1. I've read this about 4 or 5 times ( perhaps even more ) ever since I first borrowed a copy from my aunt almost a decade or so ago. It was perfect and heart wrenchingly romantic. It's as much a timeless classic as this wonderful old song, whose lyrics are perhaps most suitable for the tale that McNaught unfolds in this novel:<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MnUMzgIkf-w&amp;list=LLEt9q8AM7zjCnBQJll-Y4xQ&amp;index=0">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MnUMz...</a><br><br>Each time I re-read this novel, I am captivated by the absolute romantic splendor that's filled with angst, comedy, tragedy, drama that befits a soap opera and most of all: a second chance tale of love lost and found again. And, each time I read this again, I'm always in a rush to finish whatever chores I'm doing, just so that I can get back to the tale of Ian and Elizabeth:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1526275427ra/25535462.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ian Thornton, the H, is my #1 H of all time. In my mind, he's the H to top all others:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1526275427i/25535465._SY540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ian's the grandson of the Duke of Stanhope but he has relinquished his claim to that legacy because his grandfather had disowned Ian's family after the H's father chose to marry an ordinary Scottish girl. Ian doesn't need his grandfather's money or title, though, because he's a genius who has far more wealth than most of the Ton can begin to imagine. The H met the heroine Elizabeth at a country house party years ago during her debutante season and he was filled with insta-love for the beautiful young noblewoman:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1526275427i/25535464._SY540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Elizabeth is the belle of her Season and she received many marriage proposals from her adoring admirers, but there was only one whom her mercenary brother favoured: Viscount Moundevale. But, there was a viper in residence at the house party and that creature went by the name of Valerie. Valerie was also a plain debutante who pretended to be the heroine's friend and was jealous of all the attention that Viscount Moundevale gave to Elizabeth. This led the jealous young woman to engineer a scheme that would ensure Elizabeth's fall from grace. It was one of the saddest part of the story because it involved a pair of forged notes that led the MC's to meet each other at a cosy cottage out in the back of the estate, bordering the woods by the lake. It all blows up in their faces, Elizabeth is ruined, Ian offers to marry her because he's in love but her nasty brother challenges him to a duel. The story begins a few years after all this drama went down and the heroine's brother has "disappeared". Her guardian is now her miserly, wicked uncle who's determined to marry her off to the highest bidder. One of the men on her uncle's list is an obese, old pervert called Sir Francis Belhaven and this horrid old man has got his ugly sights set on the heroine. His intentions are nefarious, scary and gross. Elizabeth is horrified !<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1520616569ra/25188143.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved how the MC's are brought together again in a simple cottage way up in the highlands of Scotland. The H is a perfect cad who thinks Elizabeth is a flirty gold digger, so he is mean and nasty. I don't know why I still love Ian above all other H's. I think if I'd read this novel for the first time as an adult, my perceptions might be slightly different. Perhaps it's sentimentality that makes me warm to him so much even though he behaves like an ass to the heroine while they're in the secluded cottage in Scotland. I think it's all due to the magic of McNaught's writing. She has a special way with words and is the queen of heart wrenching and wrecky drama. She also manages to infuse lots of humour into situations that should be depressing. I admired the spunky heroine for the way she persevered and fought to hold on her beloved home, Havenhurst. Elizabeth was a proud, compassionate and strong character but she did have her TSTL moments too. Ian's proud and filled the need for revenge because he thinks that Elizabeth had spurned his offer of marriage all those years ago. When they meet again in Scotland, Ian's on the verge of proposing a marriage of convenience to some boring daughter of an Earl. <br><br>McNaught is one of the few authors who also manages to create some wonderfully unforgettable minor characters who are crafted with such care that one can help but love them. Two of these are: Lucinda Throckmorton-Jones ( Elizabeth's eccentric, grouchy, sourpuss but loving chaperone ) and Ian's uncle Duncan ( a priest who plays the central role in reconciling the MC's ). The MC's attraction for each other is as strong as it ever was but each is still filled with bitterness based on the lies and misconceptions from the past. It's only after Elizabeth leaves Scotland that Ian's uncle Duncan tells him the truth. Lucinda Throckmorton-Jones had been injured and in her laudanum filled state she managed to reveal everything about Elizabeth's past and current problems. Ian was shocked and desperate to make it up to the woman he loved. That's the part of the novel that I loved the most. Ian's grovelling was epic ! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1526275427ra/25535463.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ian does what many other H's never have to do: he lowers his pride for her sake and sacrifices his integrity by reconciling with the grandfather he hates. He does this this because he has to save Elizabeth from a forced marriage to the nasty Sir Francis Belhaven and because the heroine's uncle would only give her to the man with the highest title. Ian therefore resigns himself to accepting his legacy as the marquess heir of the Duke of Stanhope:<br><br><i>“That title is within your power, Ian. I realize how deep your hatred for your grandfather goes, but it no longer signifies. Either you let Elizabeth wed this despicable man Belhaven, or you reconcile with the Duke of Stanhope. It’s one or the other, and you know it.” <br><br>Ian tensed, his mind locked in furious combat against the idea of reconciling with his grandfather. Duncan watched him, knowing the battle raging inside him, and he waited in an agony of suspense for Ian to make his decision. He saw Ian bend his dark head, saw him clench his hands into fists. When at last he spoke, his infuriated curse was aimed at his grandfather: <br><br>“That miserable son of a bitch!” he bit out between clenched teeth. “After eleven years he’s going to have it his way. And all because I couldn’t keep my hands off her.”</i><br><br>Judith McNaught. Almost Heaven (Kindle Locations 4315-4321). Pocket Books. Kindle Edition. <br><br>The hero bent over backwards to ensure that all the wrongs done to Elizabeth in the past had been righted. He even ensured that the jealous junior hagwitch Valerie got her comeuppance when he gave her the social <b>cut</b> at a ball by telling her that she'd misspelled the word "greenhouse" in the notes she'd sent to him and Elizabeth all those years ago. I also laughed at Valerie because after all these years, and all her conniving, she's still single and salivating after Viscount Mondevale who doesn't seem interested in her. Ian also proves his love for Elizabeth by protecting her from her horrible uncle Julius:<br><br><br><i>“Certainly,” Julius said, his face reddening with anger. “I have it, but you’re not changing one word, and I’m not giving back one shilling.” Rounding on Elizabeth, he continued, “He paid a fortune for you, you conceited little slut –” <br><br>Ian’s savage voice cracked like a whiplash. <br>“Get out!” <br><br>“Get out?” Julius repeated furiously, “I own this house. You didn’t buy it when you bought her.” <br><br>Without looking at Elizabeth, Ian snapped a question at her, “Do you want it?” Although Julius didn’t yet recognize the depth of Ian’s fury, Elizabeth saw the taut rage emanating from every line of his powerful frame, and fear raced up her spine.<br><br> “Do I-I want what?” <br><br>“The house!” <br><br>Elizabeth didn’t know what he wanted her to say, and in the mood he was in, she was actually terrified of saying the wrong thing. Lucinda’s voice turned every head but Ian’s as she eyed him with cool challenge. <br><br>“Yes,” she said. “She does.” Ian accepted that as if the woman spoke for Elizabeth, his gaze still boring through Julius. <br><br>“See my banker in the morning,” he clipped murderously. “Now get out!” Belatedly, Julius seemed to realize that his life was in genuine jeopardy, and he picked up his hat and started for the door.</i><br><br>Judith McNaught. Almost Heaven (Kindle Locations 5626-5638). Pocket Books. Kindle Edition. <br><br>I do admit that there was one part of the novel that was filled with some unwelcome drama. The MC's got married and were finally happy when the old specter of her evil brother Robert returned to destroy things for them. I disliked Elizabeth in this part of the story because her idiocy and inability to trust the man she loved almost ruined her marriage. There was some OTT drama where she faked her death, Ian was the suspect in her "murder", she returned to clear his name, he punished her by ignoring her for a few weeks etc. I felt that part was a bit too much and ordinarily it would have made me reduce my rating for the novel. However, McNaught managed to get back into my good books by the very beautiful reconciliation scene that she wrote. In this scene, it was the heroine's turn to grovel and I loved seeing how turnabout was great fair play. I think that's what made the novel so splendid for me: in the space of one story, I got to see instances where each MC had to bend over backwards to prove how much he/she loved the other. That's what's stood out for me in this story because true love is one in which both partners are willing to do whatever it takes to make amends and right the wrongs that have been committed. The reconciliation scene occurs in the Scottish cottage once again and the author's ability to craft pure romance out of mere words is once again obvious:<br><br><i>Stroking her hair, he swallowed and spoke, but his voice was shattered. “I love you,” he said, telling her what she had told him that terrible day in his study. “I never stopped loving you.” She raised her face to his, and her answer made his chest ache. “I know.” <br><br>“How did you know, sweetheart?” he asked, trying to smile. <br><br>“Because,” she said, “I wanted it so badly to be true, and you’ve always given me everything I wanted. I couldn’t believe you wouldn’t do it, just one more time. Just once more.” She moved slightly and Ian checked her, tightening his arms. <br><br>“Stay still, darling.” he whispered tenderly, and seeing her confusion, he told her, “because our child is being conceived."<br><br> Her eyes searched his. “Why do you think so?” <br><br>“Because,” he said, slowly smoothing her hair off her cheek, “I want it so badly to be true, and you’ve always given me everything I wanted.” A lump of emotion swelled in Ian’s chest as she pressed closer against him, cradled in his arms, not moving. She was willing it to be true; he knew it as surely as he knew that, somehow, it was.</i><br><br>Judith McNaught. Almost Heaven (Kindle Locations 8179-8189). Pocket Books. Kindle Edition. <br><br>That scene and those words might be a bit cheesy but it's cheesy wonderful ! It appeals to the my romantic side and makes me sigh with wonder whenever I read this novel. McNaught also added a grand cast of characters like the MC's ( and their relatives ) from her other great love story <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/129616.Something_Wonderful__Sequels___2_" title="Something Wonderful (Sequels, #2) by Judith McNaught" rel="nofollow noopener">Something Wonderful</a>, who made cameo appearances. It was splendid to see Jordan, Alexandra, the sour dowager duchess and cousin Tony again. This novel also has one of the best epilogues that I've ever come across in a romance novel. In this novel, the author creates her magic by highlighting why the title of her novel is so significant to the story. Ian is having a conversation with his 6 yr old genius son Jonathan about the definition of <i>heaven</i>:<br><br><br><i>Crouching down, he put his arm around the little boy’s shoulders and gestured toward the garden. As if Elizabeth and Caroline sensed that they were being observed, they both looked up at the terrace, and then they smiled and waved – two green-eyed girls with gilded hair and love shining in their eyes. “In my opinion,” Ian solemnly confided to his son, “that is heaven, right there.” <br><br>“There are no angels,” Jon noted. <br><br>“I see two of them,” his father quietly replied, then he glanced at his son and amended with a grin, “three of them.” The little boy nodded slowly, a smile of comprehension drifting across his face. Turning to look up at the tall man beside him, he said, <br><br>“You think heaven will have whatever a person most wants it to have, is that it?” <br><br> “I think it’s very possible.” <br><br>“So do I,” Jon agreed after another moment’s thought. He started to turn, saw his tutor and his relatives looking expectantly in his direction, then he turned back to his father and said with a helpless smile, <br><br>“They’re going to ask what you said. And if I tell Mr. Twindell you said heaven will be like this, he’ll be very disappointed. He’s counting, you know, on gold streets and angels and horses with wings.” <br><br>“I see where that could be a problem,” Ian agreed, and he tenderly laid his hand against his son’s cheek. “In that case, you can tell him I said this is <b>almost heaven</b>.”</i><br><br>Judith McNaught. Almost Heaven (Kindle Locations 8384-8392). Pocket Books. Kindle Edition.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3141084665909108619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11053483579659303190">Going back to other books I've read from this author I feel like I'm still holding grudges against Clayton, Jason, and Jordan. Their actions against their partners were horrible. I found them way too ruthless, but their stories were compelling enough to enthrall me to the very end. Almost Heaven is a long book, 475 pages long, and I stopped reading it at page 370. The writing, as always with McNaught, was brilliant. And even though I found Elizabeth's character (unlike other McNaught's more inte</span>
  <span id="freeText11053483579659303190" style="display:none">Going back to other books I've read from this author I feel like I'm still holding grudges against Clayton, Jason, and Jordan. Their actions against their partners were horrible. I found them way too ruthless, but their stories were compelling enough to enthrall me to the very end. Almost Heaven is a long book, 475 pages long, and I stopped reading it at page 370. The writing, as always with McNaught, was brilliant. And even though I found Elizabeth's character (unlike other McNaught's more interesting heroines) shallow and predictable, the story was interesting enough to keep me engaged. Sadly, the main character's immensely stupid action made me dislike her so terribly, and my annoyance with her idiocy was such, that I lost interest in a book in which I'd had invested so much of my time. Bah!!!!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8505053019497345125"> <b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><b>Overall Opinion: </b>This was yet another enjoyable historical romance by Ms. McNaught! I liked the characters, their banter, and their connection. I also enjoyed the glimpses of the other mcs since they were side characters in this one. My biggest gripe is that it seemed very familiar. The storyline seemed to follow the same general path that the other two I read of hers recently did. Not to say they were exactly alike, but there were definitely major similarities. I guess I wanted a litt</span>
  <span id="freeText8505053019497345125" style="display:none"> <b>3.5 Stars</b><br /><br /><b>Overall Opinion: </b>This was yet another enjoyable historical romance by Ms. McNaught! I liked the characters, their banter, and their connection. I also enjoyed the glimpses of the other mcs since they were side characters in this one. My biggest gripe is that it seemed very familiar. The storyline seemed to follow the same general path that the other two I read of hers recently did. Not to say they were exactly alike, but there were definitely major similarities. I guess I wanted a little more variety and that ending wasn’t my favorite either. Overall, it was enjoyable but not one of my favorites.<br /><br /><b>Brief Summary of the Storyline: </b> This is Elizabeth and Ian’s story. They meet when Elizabeth is being presented to society at a ball. Elizabeth is a Countess and her brother is in debt and in desperate need for her to find a wealthy suitor, and Ian isn’t all that interested in those with titles since he is often snubbed by them for how he has attained his wealth. Neither of them can deny the connection they instantly feel towards one another, but their encounter ends with a duel and a ruined reputation. Years later, they meet in an unexpected way and the sparks fly again. There is some family drama, some misunderstandings, and a few sexy times...and they get a HEA ending.<br /><br /><b>Point Of View (POV):</b> This alternated between focusing on mainly Elizabeth and Ian in 3rd person narrative.<br /><br /><b>Overall Pace of Story: </b> Good. It was another long one at 517 pages in my kindle app, but it didn’t really feel that way. I thought it flowed well and I never skimmed.<br /><br /><b>Instalove:</b> Kind of. They are instantly drawn to one another and they claim that it was love instantly (later).<br /><br /><b>H (Hero) rating:</b> 4 stars. Ian. I liked him. I liked how he didn’t hesitate to tell the h how he felt.<br /><br /><b>h (heroine) rating:</b> 4 stars. Elizabeth. I liked her. I appreciated her strength and how she handled all the blows she got.<br /><br /><b>Sadness level: </b>Low, no tissues needed<br /><br /><b>Push/Pull:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ They both push away and also pursue the relationship at times. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Heat level:</b> Mild. They have some mild tension, chemistry, and scenes -- but not so much it takes away from the story.<br /><br /><b>Descriptive sex:</b> Yes<br /><br /><b>OW (Other Woman)/OM (Other Man) drama:</b> Mild jealousies <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ See cheating spoiler below <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Sex scene with OW or OM:</b> No <br /><br /><b>Cheating: </b> Not IMO<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There was mention of him snubbing the h with escorting an OW out of a party, but it is never really addressed or fully explained again (this happens after they’ve been married). The H is betrothed to OW when they meet for the second time and he decides he wants to marry the h, but that betrothal was more of a business arrangement and he doesn’t have feelings for her. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Separation:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They are separated a few times shortly (up to 3 months in one case), but there was no mention or suggestion of other partners during this time.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Possible Triggers: </b>Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The H is ~10 years (?) older than the h, the h is a virgin, and an abusive family member (off page) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Closure: </b> This had alright closure with what I would call a HEA ending <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[they’re married with children <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I didn’t like, however, how the conflict was resolved so quickly and then we went instantly into their epilogue....but that’s just a pet peeve of mine — I’m sure others would be fine with this ending.<br /><br /><b>Safety:</b> This one should be <u>Safe</u> for most safety gang readers<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have cheating (see above)<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have a descriptive sex scene with OW/OM<br />- <b> Does</b> have both the h and H pushing away<br />- <b> Does</b> have a few separations between the h and H<br />- <b> Does Not</b> have abuse by mcs<br />- <b>Does </b> have a HEA ending <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_219157508" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/219157508" />
    <a title="Jana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2296903-jana"><img alt="Jana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1387230362p2/2296903.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/219157508?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jana" href="/user/show/2296903-jana">Jana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780671742553" href="/book/show/534564.Almost_Heaven">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2296903-jana?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer219157508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11467495680487464219">It's very typical Judith McNaught, still very different from the rest of her books. Ian for instance isn't English, but 'brutal Scot' and just because he's Scot seemed like McNaught saved all of her best words and emotions for this man. But like in most of her books, her dialogues are so beautifully written that are you pulled into her world, with this book even more because English ton doesn't approve showing public emotions, Ian approves them very much. Dialogues between him and Elisabeth who </span>
  <span id="freeText11467495680487464219" style="display:none">It's very typical Judith McNaught, still very different from the rest of her books. Ian for instance isn't English, but 'brutal Scot' and just because he's Scot seemed like McNaught saved all of her best words and emotions for this man. But like in most of her books, her dialogues are so beautifully written that are you pulled into her world, with this book even more because English ton doesn't approve showing public emotions, Ian approves them very much. Dialogues between him and Elisabeth who is a true gem as well left me in awe, because there is this special connection that I feel most of the time when I read McNaught's books and I don't know how she does it. She is so mature and effortless writer. <br /><br />Ian is definitely the proudest man I have encountered in this genre, but he as well had something that I hadn't seen before: a happy and normal upbringing. Writing it like this black on white, it doesn't sound like something special, but in this genre where all men are dangerous alphas, he is alpha with irresistible signature. It's his awareness, bluntness, softness, emotional intelligence and how properly smart this man really is. His perceptions are flawless, he gets under your skin after a few pages because you don't expect some of the things that he does, but again that's why he's so different: his roots alienate him from the previous McNaught stories. I mean most of rouges in this genre are brain gifted, but I guess I liked him more than the rest was because he was so believable. His maturity was touching and this guy was normal, considering the setting. <br /><br />And his pace with Elisabeth was incredible. <br /><br />I love the floatness of this story and how simple and understandable everything was. And it's actually the only book that I read so far that wrote against the British ton: that it's not as perfect as this genre wants us to see it, it gave me blacker vision of that society. It seemed very accurate, with its unbelievably cruel rules if you are not playing for the same team. <br /><br />Yeah, definitely almost heaven experience. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11467495680487464219" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_325601966" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/325601966" />
    <a title="Esther " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9345651-esther"><img alt="Esther " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1488231133p2/9345651.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/325601966?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Esther " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Esther " href="/user/show/9345651-esther">Esther </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
